Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 And those of our time, place on a small compress generously with egg whites.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, as some people have very hard nails, you must use an instrument called "albert," of which this is the shape.
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 And so we pierce the conjunctiva only slightly, not too deeply but making it subtle, then apply egg white as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare an agreeable bed for the patient to lie on their back in a dimly lit room; advise them to be still from all movements, provide light foods easily digestible, do not move their head or arms, keep them immobilized according to their condition until three days have passed; then discharge them into the same darkened house and inspect their eyes, let them see various things, and then reattach the ligature for seven more days; it is necessary that you perform this at a time other than during the treatment or immediately after incision because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 If an abscess bursts forth, on the seventh day, drain the pus and apply soothing ointment; once it is calmed, remove the dressing from its face and wrap with a cloth for several days, remaining in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then the swelling gradually decreases and resolves into its cases; know that no apprentices should interfere in this matter.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one day among us who was from Yrach said that we were making an alchemical perception in which water flows, but I have never seen any such thing in our land nor read of it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps this is a novelty.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are resembles of forms of alchemy because those who do not know them see them as such; and they are essentially rain.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the head of these has three sharp corners.
de la char sor le neis	From the chariot onto the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 At no time do various types of abscesses arise or become swollen like scorpions with stinging tails; and if there are such ones that have flesh colored heads, and they have yellowish-colored marrow.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In the case of those abscesses that are yellowish and not filled with flesh, it is proper to make the patient sit between your hands towards the sun; clean their nostrils, and pour oil on those swellings, then press them out with a furrowed stick on one side until you know that all of the bone has been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If anything remains that cannot be covered, operate on it with all the subtle instruments lightly, ensuring nothing is left; and if it swells or forms an abscess, treat as necessary; and if malignant abscesses occur, promptly cauterize until they are closed off and excised completely, then pour oil, vinegar, or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If it is not working and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is sane; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, recognize that there is charcoal in the bone above, which prevents the swelling from coming to cut: then you must tie a bit of linen thread slightly thickened, and let our hands be between each space or less; place the patient's head through the knot at their neck as far as possible, and draw gently until it emerges into the mouth; this method is often used with children in schools, and it is an easy task for those who wish to do so; then hold the head that comes out of the neck with one hand, and the other head coming out of the mouth with the other hand, and compare each to our thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do what you know will restore the lost color, then treat the child with a thread, draw out the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian unguent, and return it to its place as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments dissolve all that is stuck from dye; and then apply a plunger of linen without any delay until healed, and if there is need for dry medicines, use them; this is the method of the instrument used to purge the head, by which one distills oils and medicines into it.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And to the les cestement, si quoi de tout en la peignez si que li se euis le santeur nus sontes ce; et neis une gist cue vunt à un peu est lour oeirent fassaint les chiefs.
de la char sor le neis	From the chariot onto the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" appears on the neck; it grows and becomes quite large to be visible by sight. Therefore, you must cut away from the beginning, completely removing any remaining tissue with surgical cautery or burning medicine. If not removed while still small, if it is hard, discolored, and has poor sensation: do not touch it with iron as it is an incurable ulcer that worsens when incised; however, if the ulcer is soft to the touch without discoloration and you can see that it can be fully excised, then proceed without fear of pain for the patient, and heal other dry and constricting areas.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the neck is cut into pieces and removed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Believes that when a solution of continuous bleeding occurs in any of these delicate bones, it benefits little, for some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then accordingly if it happens to anyone, check if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then close the two edges together with a stitch, and treat until they are healed; and if the edges are detached on both sides, ensure that you scrape off all parts of their skin until they heal, then bring the two edges together with a stitch, bind it, and powder over blood powder from a dragon's tooth, and burn incense; and place over the powders a piece of lead or other cementing substance, leaving it so that it drips by itself, then treat with ointment until they are healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way to suture it is as follows: you assemble the ends together - either with needles, as I have described in the abdomeincisions; or with thread, as I previously instructed you.
des apostemes des levres	In treating lip abscesses.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	When dense abscesses occur resembling grains of pepper, some smaller and larger; then it is necessary to return the edges, cut above each one, take with forceps and cover in each part; afterwards place the leather after vitriol incision broiling until the wound is closed; and then bandage loosely, healing the leather of dryness until it becomes healthy.
de la char des gencives	From the charring of gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often there is charring of the gums that the ancients called "albulus"; if it needs to be supported with forceps, and covered at its root, and let out the pussywire or blood flows; then place at the site vitriol incision broiling, and other desiccant powders; and if healing comes again after the cauterization, and often the second time, and the wounds. And these are of forms of treatment: it does not come to close by-soie;
des sordens	From soreness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	There are no soreness gathered at the top of the gums, between the gums and the teeth, which are unsightly and sharp; nor do the teeth ever become black or yellow with spots, as long as corruption comes to the gums, causing them to smell foul; if it is necessary that you make the patient sit with his head in your hand, and his teeth be under your holy cloth, and pull out any teeth or rough edges that appear, until there is nothing left; and thus cause darkness and greenness, and yellowness and other discolorations, as long as they are healed; and if you remove what has been the first reason, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, until you have removed all of them; and know that teeth require various forms of remedies to be cured, according to how their work shows itself, because those barbers who are unsuccessful at extracting teeth have different shapes than those used between the teeth; and these shapes and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when curing the teeth of their pain that you delay with tearing as long as possible, because it must not always be done; for this is a matter so high until there is no excuse to extract them.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient is suffering from strained teats, one must be certain of the toothache.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Many times the patient feels great pain, and believes it to be an abscess or a sore tooth; so they extract the bad tooth. Nevertheless, the pain does not go away for this reason alone, until the sickness subsides, as we have already done with such cases; and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary to cauterize around the tooth thoroughly, fortifying the gums on all sides. Then move the tooth back and forth slightly using delicate forceps until properly aligned, then firmly secure the tooth with forceps; ensuring the head of the patient's sick side between your knees, so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth properly and breaking it, if it does not come out easily, take any of these substances and apply them within each piece gently; then move it as you did initially.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and filled with thread where the roots are; and if it is gently pulled out with pincers, so that it does not break when removed; and one must work skillfully around the gums in order to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And ensure that it is not broken and a part remains; returning to the patient with greater pain due to the root's evil nature.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And be aware not to do as ignorant barbers who, due to their haste and boldness, often break the cartilage without performing what we have described; instead, they bring great disease through the oozing of roots or by breaking the cartilage, as we have seen often; and when a tooth is pulled, cleanse its socket with wine or oil and seal it; if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the socket with vitriol paste; and if that doesn't work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the strumas are where teeth move first, with long points and large mats, do not double when you pull them; these are the shapes.
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of large teeth such that they do not bend while pulling, and be well-crafted of iron, and have teeth to grip when pulled.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the spine
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains in place after treatment, it is necessary to put a soft cloth soaked in butter on it for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 As long as the wound is healing, use these pliers called "algèfre", which make it appear like a surgeon's beak. And within them are shaped like a file and that's its form:

et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools in front of him for teeth, and from this instrument that looks like large pincers, the form it takes is as follows:

Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	Let them be large and well-held for grasping the bone, so it does not escape but can hold and extract; then restore to its place with appropriate medicines, and if there is putrefaction in the bone, and it is small, you possess all this instrument.

et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is similar to the shaping of needles; and in filing the tooth, do so piece by piece over time gently, until it no longer moves when bitten; then smooth it out completely at the end with a razor-sharp finish, and if it's too sharp causing bleeding on the tongue, file down the harshness until even, so that it neither cuts the tongue nor corrupts speech.
quant li dent lochent	Whenever the tooth chips
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the teeth are loose or broken by impact or fall, and the patient cannot press down on what they chew without saliva flowing from them, cure them with medicines that restrict movement, but this does not work; instead, restrain it with a gold thread because silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes. The thickness of the wire should be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, depending on the space between the teeth; if you see any teeth moving towards each지, take the wire and double it up between the two healthy teeth, then place the chisel between the teeth as many as there are, until securely positioned to a stable adjacent tooth. Then continue covering back to where you started, gently but skillfully pulling the wire without movement; ensure your knot is firm at the root of the loose tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then clamp the head of the bone with pliers, and join them together, positioning between the healthy teeth so that it does not affect the tongue; then leave it as tightly closed as it can remain, and if dislocated, or the threads come loose, be restrained by another thread; if it stays in place, it will serve for its entire life, forming the shape of two healthy teeth and the appearance of just-set bones.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens. Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 Those who have no head, like a superficial abscess, you must pierce it easily; and when the abscess is large and has great swelling, and you pierce it, do not pull out all the pus at once, but drain one part; then bandage the abscess until the next day, then avoid draining anything further; repeat this process gradually larger each time, until all the pus is gone; especially if the patient is weak in strength, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the arrow can sometimes leap out with the release of the bowstring, and inadvertently kill the patient, so be cautious.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Treat this chapter with great caution, and when you perceive the abscess, open the wound, and examine if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it's a clean cut, stitch it with linen or old cotton; and if it's large abscesses, and there are many threads, ensure that in each you place a tent so they come together; and if you have sewn around part of the skin within the abscess, fill it with old cotton or wool from linen cloth without moisture, up to three days; then unsew it, and apply ointment until healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 If bleeding occurs on your wound, treat with cold water and ease, and moist cloth, and place it on the affected area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If bleeding persists, treat properly and heal, and the powders I have mentioned in this book, apply with warm wine or oil; and if it is winter time, and the affected area or abscess is very sensitive, cover it with tents and moistened cloths soaked in wine or hot oil; and if it is summer, and the affected area is thick, cover it with moistened cloths in cold water or oil or warm vinegar until the third day as we have said, then drain the abscess and express and heal according to necessity until it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is how one must generally proceed in the treatment of abscesses: but I have told you how to approach treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	Of pus-filled collections.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 When small abscesses arise in the scalp, they are handled as silk, similar to the follicles of a girl's hair, and there are many like this.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that have fat and texture like hairs with moisture; and there are others that are hard and painful to the touch at the base, and there is no doubt if the arrow hits contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the techniques of bandaging are such that you must try with all instruments called 'entromissors', from which formations come afterwards and what they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 Because if it contains moisture, it grows above the long one. (This could refer to a growth or formation that occurs when there is an excess of moisture.)
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 When the moisture is drained, scrape without leaving any hair that contains it, as it returns as soon as you leave it alone; then immerse cotton in Egyptian ointment if available; if not, use water and salt, and apply to the wound, and let it remain until the next day; these will heal those who have been afflicted all night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the abscess remains fatty, then follow this method for long: drain it and wash with vinegar, and scrape off all parts, and apply all your treatment to where it is located; and if an arrow causes opposition, do as I have instructed you previously.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And similarly treat an abscess if it is pus-filled, and with scraping and cleaning as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And the treatment of a pus-filled abscess and its moisture is easier, for it contains less blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if some of these abscesses or in the head have no moisture, and among these I found an abscess similar to a long stone: hard, sharp, and dirty; and had it been struck by anyone, they would have made a wound like from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses or in the head, for those that come from children's heads and ear roots, let the opening be made highest at the most dependent point to allow pus to exit; and treat them as it is due.
des scrophules	Of scrofulous tumors
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and from under the shoulders, and in the armpits, and never come to any other place or body parts, and they are very much, and closely connected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and others that hold malicious intentions which do not wish to obey healthiness.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois. And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work on it, then put vitriol paste in the wound, or any powders that cause bleeding, and bind the wound; let it remain until the abscess is soothed and softened, and begins to decay.

And when the abscess is healed, return to your work until completed; then use thy ointment and bandages if there are any small ulcers remaining, cover and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein at the root of the ulcer, do not cut that ulcer to its root but bind it with a strong double thread and let it hang by itself without harm; then apply the wound with fine cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure.

si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 And it is necessary for you to bind up the root and drain pus, and close as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez. de squinance	If you are treated by applying a tissues to ensure there's no longer remains of any dead tissue, then as we had said previously mentioned, so forth; and when the wound with substances so is that healing ointment and other until it properly cleaned becomes cured.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and talked about the treatment of the throat; but I have never seen in our land that it is made, and this is according to their writings.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with strangulation, it is necessary that the fracture of the throat called "epiglote" be removed; and this cannot heal by itself because all the veins and the main source of pain are present in those who have abscesses hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in two almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the main source, it is necessary to remove the epiglote to avoid destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 It is therefore necessary when we wish to split the epiglottis that we split it from above three circles or four with a small cut across, between two circles or by the quantity of the cut on the side, not in the cartilage; and those locks are suitable for sectioning the epanglottis such that there is no sound, and the blades are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is fearful, then he should extend the skin of the throat to its full length, and split it up to where it joins with the trachea; squeeze out any blood vessels, provided you see nothing there, and then close the fistula as we have said; and demonstrated by the cutting of the membrane of the trachea which breaks open at the place that is ruptured, and due to loss of voice; leave the open wound closed for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed for which there is doubt of strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound near the cheek, and tie a bandage that tightly presses against the jawbone; then apply medicines that induce warmth until it becomes healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	the uzerd: and  (or they:s.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then take the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and they breathe through the wound, thus preventing death; and therefore it is commanded to leave the open wound until the sickness has passed, which takes three or four days, after which you are ordered to sew up the wound and treat it, until it is healed; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a maiden took a knife and stabbed it into her throat, cutting the left side of her larynx; and I went to call for help to cure her, but found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I examined the wound and found that blood had come from it; however, she hadn't bitten a vein or other tissue, just her throat, and the blood flow was coming through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurried to sew up the wound and treat it until healed; and it happened that the maiden recovered enough to have a red voice again, returning to her normal self; therefore I say there is no need for fear in the treatment of the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 These abscesses are called "throat hernia," and they are large abscesses with the color of jet, predominantly in women; there are two ways: natural and accidental, where the natural has no means.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accidental way has two types: one resembling fat-like matter and another type of abscess that comes from us like an artery; there is fear, and it does not need to be treated with fire unless it is small, and test and examine everything thoroughly: if you find it similar to fatty substance, and without attaching to any vein, wrap as one would bandage a wound, and treat the entire area until fully healed.
des nous	And let us know.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 There are many ways to address this, all which I shall describe their resemblances; and now it is necessary for me to explain the entire difference that exists between them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that fever and inflammation are present until the boiling over is past, and the putrefaction is complete; then rests the fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With ours, there is neither fever nor pain and it contains pus, which is its own sac and corresponds to the body's color, beginning similarly to glass, and becomes larger; and they correspond to two appearances, either hard or moist, and very much in accordance with what I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the care of us that you first examine and inquire about all the instrument called "intermitted", according to its form or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the method of inquiry for abscesses in us is that you grasp or make it more moist than you find within the abscess, and turn your two fingers slowly until you know that the pus has been felt by the touch, then proceed according to the size of the abscess; then extract the foreign body, and be cautious so as not to hurt.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs in a vein and it has such color as I have mentioned regarding other abscesses; and if after the incision no moisture comes, consider it fatty, treat then accordingly with cross cuts, grasping at each end and carefully scraping from all sides, ensuring the skin is healthy using a needle; and if you cannot render it clean in one piece, slice it so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 If there remains nothing, it returns many times; and if some portion lingers causing slight pain, apply the wound with corrosive ague powders, press the wound, and place soothing substances over it, treating other ailments until healed; and if significant swelling occurs, cut along the edges of the wound, and treat as that which causes fever.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the pus is thick or contrary in any way, hasten and mix it with white vitriol paste, and leave it for two days or three, until the wound dries out, then let the sanguineous effervescence rest; afterwards return to sewing what was left undone.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 See the forms of entwined strands, and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small; and among them there are three types called "albaret," and one type called "breb," and there are also three sizes: large, medium, and small, to search for fistula boils; they resemble the needles used in sorcery, made of citron wood or iron, or silver, with yellow ones being effective, while black ones are more suited for searching for cerebrus from a fistula; they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the opening.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The forms of tumors come in various shapes, as you can see: large, medium, and small; if there are tumors with two types of boils each; if there are tumors with three types of boils, and they also come in three kinds; if there are tumors with two types of boils, or just one type only, and these all come in three sizes; and all these must be present at their location.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The chief of these tools are sharp, and among them there are those that cut only from one side, where the skin is scraped but not severing vein or nerve; and among the intermediaries are those reset in clamps, so that the patient does not feel it at the opening of abscesses. There are three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one should never use them if fully extended, such as legs, arms, hands, elbebows, and similar areas; and never is another instrument used, like incisions resembling fistulas, according to this method, through which blood is channeled.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed at no time back into its proper position of veins and arteries, and does not return according to this grand form.

Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it breaks immediately and falls out with the urine, and the patient is relieved; if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then thread another wire under the stone on both sides, make a hole in the rod at the place of the stone between two ties, then extract it forcefully, break the tie, and cleanse the frozen blood present in the wound; cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stones

Sometimes stones are inserted in women and if it happens even once, the treatment is difficult, and there are three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman may be a virgin; and the second reason is that no woman can properly find another who knows how to undress at the mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. de hernie carnouse	For a carnous hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non. de l’aposteme des coions	Then cauter la le plasters tale of les art, dont the bleu:

des hermofrodites	Hermaphroditism refers to a condition where an individual has both male and female reproductive organs or characteristics of both sexes. This term was derived from Greek mythology, referring to the deity Hermes/Mercury, who was born with combined features of his parents Zeus (the sky god) and Hermah (a nymph). In modern times, it is considered an outdated and potentially offensive term; preferred terms are intersex or transgender.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine. Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other manner is in women, and it is above their wrist like a rod and two hoops.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment of men and women is that you remove all swellings on their wrists as well as other injuries; in the second manner, for men whose urine leaks through the skin between the hoops, there is no remedy.

dou fremit	In trembling

des plaies	Of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	In the section on wound treatment that we have mentioned before; now we will say about hand and medicinal treatments, according to their completion.

de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of the wound of spear or knife

And when you see good healing signs, know that the wound is saved.

Treat with bandages and other remedies until healed; and if it cannot be healed or operated upon, then determine that there is a fistula; treat accordingly as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 If the wound is a cut from a sword or knife and is simple or on the back, treat the part that is in front; if it's large, with bandages; and if small, with powder; and if embedded in bone with fragments removed as needed, treat the wound and any remaining shaft pieces accordingly. If not completely debrided, allow the wound to scar over for easier extraction; judgment on other limb injuries should be made as we have described.
