de la cuixe brisie	of a broken hip joint
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the hip joint is often broken in many ways, and when it turns forward and backward, its restoration involves applying a ligature above or below the fracture.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies face down, then each attendant extends their hands equally on all sides of his body; and this is when the fracture is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 If the fracture is near the root of the hip, let one ligament be towards the wrist and the other below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And similarly if it is near the knee, then let the ligament be by the knee and its extension; then with a mirror place the bone in equal two hands, according to its natural figure, and then place the plaster, without any abscess occurring.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess hot, let it be pacified then return to your work and care; the lanced opening is done in part by method.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 It is necessary that you wrap above the fracture with a doubled bandage in two or three layers and leave some excess; then rotate the leg until the heel reaches the root of the thigh, and put a long thread between the hip and the leg, below the knee; let the top end of the thread reach upwards; then rotate above the leg and above the hip with the bandage, then place an upright at the fracture site and another on the leg bone; then tie off the remaining space between the leg and the hip using a softer fabric to ensure even tensioning; start making three or four turns around the fracture. The more you tighten near the fracture, the less it is strained. Then go back to the two ears of thread that were put between the leg and the hip, and remove three uprights above them, then return to below the top end of the thread until you reach the foot; if it does not move from its place, leave it as such; otherwise do nothing else or don't let any abscesses or swellings occur.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens that it dislocates again, and address what is happening as we have said many times before; and if there are pieces of bone sticking out, then they must be pushed back in if possible, but if not, one can split the flesh, and extract the fragments; and the treatment should be done as we have described until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	At no time is the thigh broken as when one inserts pegs, such as in the shoulder and arm; however, with healing done this way, it does not alleviate the patient's suffering.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in one or two days, or a little more or less, depending on the variations of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the hollow of the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 It is said that in the glen of the neck there are few fractures, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if broken, it is not so much a crack or piercing, but occurs in all wounds, and causes pain, and feels very unwell.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the healing process involves setting it as equally balanced as possible with its parts moved so they can be assembled; then apply the splint, and if needed, put on a round board, and secure firmly as necessary, then address all the arrangements we have mentioned for other breaks, such as swelling and similar issues; apply to each accident what is suitable for it until healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Concerning the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 It is said that in the leg there are two bones; one called 'right' and the other called 'femur'; and all types of fractures occur as they do in the arm, and thus the treatment is similar to that of the arm entirely, and the procedures apply to both. And if the two bones break together, the leg turns at every part.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bone is shattered, then turn to face forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and swelling can be seen clearly; and it appears bent out of shape.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then make the reduction and align it properly, and secure the fragments evenly; but always, ensure there is no unsightly fracture, and if there are more pieces, that the reduction be smaller and easier; and apply a splint according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two bandages of hemped wood that wrap around the leg on both sides, and are as long as the leg from knee to ankle; then wrap them in two layers, one above and one below, and tie them securely together so the leg cannot turn left or right, and thus it is well done; and no one should administer a band of wood along the length of the leg if it is made of wood, and properly keep the leg from moving; regularly check for any swelling or other issues in the area of breakage or wound; and cure until healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Regarding the fracture of the bone of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but at the bone of the foot a break occurs sometimes and in the shinbone, and nothing happens to cause weakness or other conditions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If there is a break in the bone of the foot and you see these bones protruding from one another, place it gently on the ground as if it were going to walk, then immediately put your own foot under its, where the bones are raised; then press until they return to their places; then apply a poultice and compresses above, and place a small bandage with two plain pins below, over the belly of the affected foot, secure it temporarily, then wrap around with cloths as needed.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, you will loosen the ligament, for you will find that the bones are equal again, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are any broken bones, then repair them as we have said for the hand; then insert a splint along the length of the limb, and make it slightly wider; then place underneath the foot the table I mentioned, and stretch it immediately; and if there are two or three or more, break each one individually, placing a splint according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and secure the table beneath the leg so that its top aligns with the stomach.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary not to forget the other things I have said regarding other fractures, as we have mentioned; and treat each incident accordingly.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Regarding the fracture of the hand bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of a woman's body is broken, if she lies down with it elevated, then incline her toward the less painful side and support her behind; next fill the wound with cotton from a sick person according to your discretion; then have her stand up gradually, slowly lifting her back until the cotton reaches the entrance of the body and realigns the bone; when she needs to urinate, remove the cotton, and once she has urinaturesset it again: do this for seven or eight days: if you look after her properly, the fracture will be healed, and then take a sheepskin bladder, attach an envelope to one end, fill the entire bladder with liquid, blow air into the envelope until the bladder is empty; the wound will close again; then fill it with cotton and leave it as such for several days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the forefinger of the man is broken, or of the woman, be restored as we have said in the hip bone; and these fractures are not hidden from those who apply their study and use, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For fractures mean various conditions for the right way of restoration: so it is to be understood.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	And of the bones quant les lignons li les bone.
de brisure avec plaie	Of fracture with a wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for those who have a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large like the bone of the hip or shoulder or similar, to be healed now, as long as the sinews we mentioned confirm this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, and there remains lead poisoning, unless you have other things, then begin to restore the fracture in that same hour or day, as long as abscesses do not appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	; they can. the same:
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible above the joint, it must be gently set into place with your hands, in slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if you cannot set the extension with your hands to be level, then use this instrument made of iron, which has seven or six branches and is long in length; and its width depends on the quantity of the wound; thus it is necessary for a surgeon that he grips three or four, as needed for each fracture treatment; and let them have hooks and be somewhat thicker so they do not bend under compression to the limb at your workplace, and place them firmly in front, and thick enough forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And called "pallance," for the patient's head must be placed on the visible part of the bone; and it is done once until it returns, and they are level with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle, and the splints cannot properly take hold of the bone, then it must be cut off until the splints have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot bring back the bone as we have said, with the aid of an appropriate instrument, whether cutting or sawing, to your ability; then extract that which is lodged in the hardened bone and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is returned to its place, if the patient feels great pain afterwards, believe that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 If you return it to its place and then moisten the dressing with a stipulative black ointment, and properly so it is in shape; do not apply any cerote or other substance unless there is oil present, otherwise prevent rot and decay from occurrebi; after restoring the bones, leave the wound exposed, cover all around according to the size of the wound, ensuring that you protect well against straining with fractures; many times this has been done by madmen, resulting in death or corrosion at least once; and it should be strung more gently and softer than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is severe or large, and you doubt that something unforeseen may occur, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then it does not require placing a splint; but wrap around it, near the wound, with stiff cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one or two days that pus flows from the wound, remove what you have placed on it, and apply healing salve to the wounds, as with a four-part remedy and similar substances.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it becomes relaxed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be fitted with a splint so that the bow supports it lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if several days pass and it cannot be straightened but continues bent like this, for there are small bone fragments, you must clean the wound with gauze and remove all those unnecessary fragments that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if an abscess comes to the area, or another form of decay, it is necessary that you treat it, as described in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and exposed in the limb, like the hip or shoulder, and other similar large body parts, do not attempt to treat it, for many times death occurs, but leave it until it heals; perhaps it will be expelled by itself after twenty days or thirty, then tend to the wound if you can; and if you cannot, just let it go.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	From bruises which arise upon the saddle.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come upon the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and an ugly thing to see is the state of the limb; and sometimes it cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Be careful then if it is fresh: if you administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and frankincense, pitch, acacia, and other similar things; take any of these items or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or plenty of vineger or honey water; put it in leather pouches, strain it well, and do not untie the knot for days; then reset, and continue to another until the swelling is ossified like bone; or you may be bound with a piece of wood properly shaped; because the property of this piece of wood is that it removes all inflammation from above the limbs; if the swelling has already turned hard as stone, and needs to be removed, then cut away any excess protrusion; or take it to some barber who will pare until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, and remains weak after the limb has become frail and delicate for various reasons: one is because it was tied too tightly, and not loosened as it should be; or because there were too many bandages, preventing blood circulation to the limb; or due to a multitude of wounds; or from excessive movements at inappropriate times; or because there is little blood within its body, thus making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is to have the patient eat well and keep their body warm until there are many blood vessels in them again; and administer baths for joy and comfort; then apply plasters on the limb, so that they draw a lot of nourishment into it, and frequently re-wet with water while the circulation restores to the member; and bring back its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	After injury has healed, the limb becomes twisted
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after healing, and bones are broken openly, and the shape of the limb appears ugly, yet it still retains its natural formation: do not believe the fools who say that you must break the limb anew entirely, as many foolish people have done in our land; these practices are condemned, and they bring great harm and sometimes death. However, if dislocations and tortures are fresh, it is fitting that they be eased with hot water or soft herbs cooked, such as coltsfoot leaves, roots, meadowsweet, and similar things; and prepare a mollifying poultice, like well-made diaquilon, and take the muscatel of coltsfoot, and mix it with pig fat or oil of sesame, and apply the poult지; or take oily figs, and grind them with fennel seeds, and other medicines that soothe swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And at no time is an inflamed bone treated by continuously rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And thus, adjust the position of each limb.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the curvature is old and hardened, like stones, it needs to be removed with iron, so that it extends up to the bone using a subtle delicate saw-like instrument; then apply pressure and careful attention in its treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs, if necessary now reset without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if it is delayed, and the inflammation has spread, and when attempting to reset it takes effort; therefore, do not move the limb at the time of inflammebtion: often this causes swelling and other pains; nonetheless, once that occurs, soothe the patient's pain first, then leave them alone until the abscesses are calmed. Then immerse the limb in warm water and oil, gently exercise it, and treat each limb as needed when treatment is required at its location.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	.
des mandibules	Of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Occasionally the jawbones become dislocated and remain so; there are two ways this occurs: either they are slightly out of place but softened a bit, or completely displaced, hanging towards one side, causing saliva from the mouth to not be contained, unable to close their mouth, and wrapping around their tongue when speaking.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When dislocation is slight, it can return on its own in various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is complete and properly done, you must reset the jaw quickly without delay, and in such a way that the ointment touches the patient's head, pouring a little bit of oil from one hand into the root of the mandible dislocation inside the mouth; since the dislocation occurs on both sides. The other two hands should be equal, and instruct the patient to soften their jawbones and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And then put it inside of its place until they are balanced equally; and take your right beforehands:
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	If it is difficult to reset, especially if they are the two mandibles together, use hot water and oil, until gently realigning; do not strain in attempting to reset, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are equally returned, and the patient's mouth feels a significant softening, place them on cloths moistened with a cream made of oil rose and wax, then lightly bind it with fine threads; let the patient lie on their back, and their chin be between two pillows so that they do not move or turn left or right, nor strain to swallow but gently chew meat until pains are gone, and the jaws are thoroughly bathed; then follow what they wish easily, without forcing them to open their mouth for eating or drinking, until the mandibles are well cleansed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be reset to their place within an hour and are not returned to their original positions, fever and usual complaints may come, and perhaps abdominal issues, or possibly complete vomiting of bile alone.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then say that it is a loss; and often those who experience it die within seven days.
de la forcelle	Of the hernia
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The hernia cannot dislodge from within the ribcage and below, and it is never displaced once formed, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 The restoration is that the patient lies on their back and extends their arms; then press the form of the shoulder with your palm, and it will return; then place a pad and bandage over it, and bind it tightly; and the eye which is towards the pain cannot dislocate. If not, and if it does dislocate even once, reset to its position as we have said; then place another pad and bandage over it, and bind it firmly, and allow the patient to rest until they are healed; likewise, return the shoulder blade when displaced from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Regarding the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 That the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one way where it comes out from the ankle area; another where it comes out at the back of the leg; and occasionally coming out towards the front, which happens rarely; and not backwards nor internally by the nerves; and sometimes dislocates downwards towards the ankle, especially in those with little flesh, as it does so quickly for them; for those with enough flesh, jumps easily and re-enters easily.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes there are individuals with blows or fractures, and their shoulder swells with a hot abscess; they think it is dislocated due to this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then it is necessary for you to examine it thoroughly until certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And the dislocation is known when it goes downward towards the ankle, and there is difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their diversity evident; and at the top of the shoulder, a socket is found, and where the head of the shoulder touches the topside, just like if it were two eyes; and the patient cannot bring his hand near himself nor make any movements; and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden because you can clearly see it when touched; and this kind of dislocation is not only about resetting, especially when a child feels unwell.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is for the minister to lift the hand of the sick person upward, then place poultices under the joint and raise it forcefully to its place; the minister lifts the hand and extends it upward, placing it down again quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 If it does not come as we have said after several days, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and be made comfortable with soothing and relaxing methods, like an infusion of althea and fenugreek and millet seed in hot water, and thus prepared; then lay the patient on their back, and under the shoulder insert a strap equal in thickness, not too soft or hard, then place the foot over the strap, gently lift the head of the dislocated shoulder, and treat it with your hand; and other attendants dye the top of the injured person's head, so that it does not move forward; the shoulder returns immediately, and if you see it return according to this method: and have a man present who is larger than the patient; stand straight towards their side, and support the dislocated shoulder underneeby the neck, gently lifting it upwards so that the injured person hangs in the air; and other attendants treat the lower part of the injured person's hand toward the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 If the patient is too lightweight, accompany them with something heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And the resetting can be done in another manner: and it is as when one drives a long stake into the ground so that the shoulder returns like a pistachio, neither too large nor too thick; then it should be placed under the patient, with fabric for protection above, while the limb remains straight; then their hand is extended to the other side properly, and the joint will return to its place quickly. If it does not want to return despite all these things we have mentioned, do this treatment: take a stake two arm's length long and four palms wide, which has a head that fits for fingers to enter from one end towards the knee, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then wrap the head with a cloth so it does not touch the patient, then place under the saddle where the shoulder is, and extend your arms over the length of the staff, tie the arm to the staff at the top of the hand, then put one arm through the chest strap of a wide saddle pad, with hands facing downward, leaving the body hanging on the other side: the joint will remain in place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is set in place, however you do so, it must be that you put under the saddle a staff of woolen yarn, then apply a poultice of powdered medicine, with incense and ointment of frankincense on all around the shoulder, then tighten it away from the saddle quickly, and wrap the hand at its neck, leaving hands hanging thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	It is proper that he rests little while the member becomes comfortable, for it will recover sooner; and then rest more after 5 or 6 days, and move it; and if it is firm but not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is forced out due to moisture that caused it or another reason, you must apply three punctures with cautery as described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after 6 days, and the joint cannot stay in place or lift the arm upward, then understand that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are compressed or stretched out or weakened; and understand that the joint will never be properly placed there.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs in the leg and thigh or behind is caused by impact, extended hands, and another lever; treat until it is set right.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing come tremors in the limb and later movements, the patient uses them many times until those tremors cease, returning to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of the dislocation of the knee
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	the S; and a se; This ou tizz que c�C: est they arent; en leur ce ; by.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when joining the patient's joint properly with the healthy one, you should see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is raised and cannot bend the arm or reach its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it as quickly as possible when abscesses occur there, for if they were occurring, the repositioning would be difficult; and sometimes not at all, especially if it's towards the back; this type of dislocation is worse than others, causes greater pain, and possibly death.

The restoration is when it can be repositioned, extend its hand to your two hands; and the arms spread out, and the hands according to the proper position around it, above and below, place the joint back on its peach together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	When dislocation is before, it returns when the hand doubles to itself and the root of the palm's edge that has been dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie. Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firmly in its place, then dislocate it and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not tighten well, repeat the splinting and binding, leaving it like this for several days until it is securely set; then dislocate it again.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 If after the repositioning of the joint it feels unstable and moves, then bathe and rub well, applying pressure until soothed; or place a fat sheep grease on the joint, leave for one day and night, then reset, and let them take a bath; when they sweat, promptly rub the joint, then reapply the grease, followed by another bath; repeat this two to three times until healed; if so, apply moist whey cheese warmed with butter, and strain it on.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand joint occurs, and its return is light compared to other joints generally; it must be quickly returned to its place at the same time as it becomes dislocated again, so that swelling or pus does not occur therein.

The repositioning is done by placing the patient's hand on a table, extending their fingers, and aligning them so that they place their palm over the joint area, pressing until it returns to its normal shape; then you must check if it has been properly placed; thus, position the patient'lete back onto a table for extension and repositioning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure. Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hands are at rest, place them on the platform as we have said, then grasp and leave for 5 days, then release and let it be so.

de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of dislocation of the hand's fingers

dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	For the dislocation of the spinal column in the back

des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocation of the hip joint
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is said that hip and shoulder joints only come with dislocations, not as other joints do; the hip joint can be dislocated in four parts: anteriorly, posteriorly, internally, and externally; more often it comes out internally, less so frontwards and backwards.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is such that when you join the injured leg with the healthy one, it appears longer, and exposes more bone ends on the sick than the healthy, and the sick cannot double their hip socket in fire; and are legs that swell near a hot abscess, because the knee head comes loose.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of those for whom it occurs is that this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of those who suffer before it, are such that they extend their leg according to completion; however, do not double the knee in pain, and if one wishes them to walk, they cannot bend forward, retains urine, swells with anger, and as they walk, passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs for those who suffer behind it are such that they cannot expand their knee or double it, and the leg is more twisted than the other, anger is alleviated, and the head of the hip to its place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The signs of this type of dislocation are such that you must know if the dislocation has occurred before, and it remains according to its condition, there is no treatment; and in no way should it have arrogance.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	When the dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocating, quickly return the joint to its place, push it in and out, and move it right and left; perhaps it will return on its own without needing further care.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, you must strongly bind the limb with two hands or a tie over its hip socket; another method involves extending one's hand above so that they place their hands under their shoulders and pull tightly on a light tie at the hip; another ties the head to the tie; and all extend upwards and downwards once, until the injured is lifted off the ground once, then it hangs suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for 4 types, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is fine.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres. Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot hold it in this manner as we have said, then bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong bandage above the heels and on both knees, and let the affected leg be extended two inches more than the other; then hang them from their head using a pole, and arms outstretched for long lengths; then command one assistant to embrace the pelvis, while others are hanging with the patient, who properly embrace the pelvis, as the joint returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 When the dislocation is not in use, gently touches the patient as with those having sprains, and properly stretches near the affected limb and joints; then apply ties at the head and other places; then insert a tine between the buttocks towards the malady's location; also surround it with moistened cloth so it doesn't move, then stretch each minister outwards from him, and the mire aligns equally to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, that is well.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place on a board and press as we have said with sprains, and touch the patient near the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it should be stretched out hastily with the injured leg, and according to what I have said; place your hands on their painful side, then press with the other hand, and extend downward toward the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is in place, it should not extend the patient's arm or lift it off the ground, but instead let it lie as a hinge would have been dislocated behind; and lay on its face, with the limb extended as we have said at lying on two pillows; then apply pressure to the joint against the table; and it will be ready when the patient extends his legs, which should be even; then support the buttocks, place the heating-iron, and tighten a bandage so that the hinge does not move; and rest for three or four days before removing it; and place the heating-iron again above. And if you see them to be even, then tighten the bandage as before, and leave it for three days; then allow the patient to walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The joints are dislocated in three ways: through pressure from within and behind; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the signs are such that you command the patient to bend his leg towards his hip, and if it does not reach its hip, know that it is dislocated; and in all cases of restoration, ensure the patient sits upright, extends his leg as much as possible, and places his back on his thighs, with his foot under your feet; then take his heel in your palms, pull apart between your thumbs, then bend both sides of the heel thoroughly; other assistants extend his foot until the knee joint returns to its place, and the sign is that it gently touches its hip; apply a poultice there, then bandage the leg to the thigh, keeping them tightly together for 3 or 4 days, then release. And do not let the patient walk while the limb is still unstable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not much affected, it must be firmly supported strongly, as we have said in the treatment of the elbow, until it becomes well-aligned.
de la dislocation dou talon	Regarding ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes numb, never fully dislocated, within and without.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and try before reaching the part where it was dislocated: repositioning should be light, and extend gently with your hands when only slightly touched.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is completely dislocated, you must make the patient sit upright, and support them mainly with their leg, above the ancułe; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, then twice with your left hand, then lift upwards, and gently place the foot on top; do this twice as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, start the process again because it will return; and if it cannot be returned like this, make the patient lie down on their back on the ground, and securely insert a stick between their thighs to prevent movement of the body; then press the stick against the buttocks, and with other attendants extend the foot towards them or by its ligaments that it lies under the neck of the foot; then equally extend all attendants, and let the stick remain between the patient's thighs to keep the body still when extended; then place mirrors symmetrically on both sides of the dislocation with their hands, and other attendants pull the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it has reached its endpoint, apply the dressing and packs on top, stretch firmly, and tie the bandage around the leg, and watch for nerves located behind the ankle, so that the binding is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the binding softens, retension the wound; then release at the third day or a quarter of one, preventing the patient from moving by four days; and if they progress beyond this period, it is not without concern that it may dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes there, one must soothe it as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	From the shoulder dislocation and its treatment, let's discuss a few related matters:
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	by;t what d. If:
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any part of the back or foot, it must be made to sit straight on a level surface or table, and place your foot under where these joints are affected, then press firmly with your foot; do so until it returns; and when they are aligned properly, and there is nothing wrong, put a board beneath the sole of the foot, then retension firmly, leave for three days, then release, and let them rest until healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	For both wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When wounds come with dislocation and we see them to be healed, many times the patient dies: if you are not confident in the treatment unless you are wise in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and if you are merciful and compassionate and slow to act; do not be rash. Begin with soothing treatments for abscesses hot and leave the sick person in God's hands if there is no hope of health; and when there is hope, reset the limb now as the abscess softens; and once the limb is in place, apply calming remedangs to the abscess, and tend to the wound as needed with dried ointments. And if there is dislocation with bone fractures and small bones come out of place, follow what we have said about simple illnesses; and beware of taking a path of fear according to what I have said, for it will bring you misfortune by your Creator and because of the healthiness of your armor and body.
Amen	 Amen
